## Turn 21 — ASSISTANT — 2026-04-21T13:51:00.759Z

[TEXT]
Before I plan this out, the numbers don't match the current code and there are a few ambiguities I want to pin down. Here's the skeleton I *think* you mean, followed by questions.

## Sketch of the loop
1. **Gen 0**: generate random population of size N, score all.
2. **Each generation**:
   - Sort by fitness, keep top half (elites) — already scored, not re-evaluated.
   - Form 250 pairs from the top 500, each pair produces offspring.
   - Offspring replace the bottom half.
   - Score **only the new offspring** (cached scores for elites carry forward).
3. **Stop** when improvement over the last 100 gens is < 1%, after G ≥ 100.

## Grilling questions

1. **Population size.** Top 500 + 250 pairs replacing a bottom 500 ⇒ N = 1000. But `POPULATION_SIZE = 250` right now. Bumping to 1000? (The assignment spec is fine with this; I just want confirmation before I change the constant.)

2. **Offspring per pair.** 250 pairs × 2 children = 500 fills the bottom half exactly. Two children per pair? Or one child per pair and I need 500 pairs (with parents reused)?

3. **How are pairs chosen from the top 500?**
   - (a) Uniform random pairing — simple, but ignores fitness gradation inside the top half.
   - (b) Fitness-weighted via softmax (what the assignment actually asks for) — better performers breed more often; performers can appear in multiple pairs.
   - These give very different behavior. Which do you want?

4. **Crossover mechanism.** Per-activity, does the child inherit the entire `Assignment` (time/room/facilitator as a unit) from parent A or parent B by coin flip? Or do we mix the three fields independently? The first preserves more structure; the second explores more.

5. **Mutation.** Applied only to offspring, or also to carried-over elites? If elites mutate, we lose the "don't re-score the top 500" optimization because their genomes changed. I assume offspring-only — confirm?

6. **Mutation rate semantics.** Is `MUTATION_RATE = 0.01` a per-gene (per-assignment) probability, or per-schedule? The assignment usually treats it per-gene and decays it over generations — do you want decay now or a flat rate first?

7. **Termination.** "< 1% improvement over last 100 gens after G ≥ 100" — measured on best fitness, or average fitness? The spec is typically average, but some implementations use best.

8. **Tie-breaking in the "top 500" cut.** If fitnesses tie at the boundary, does it matter which specific schedule is kept? (Probably no, but flagging.)

Answer these and I'll write the plan out concretely.

CS 461 AI


Program 2 – Genetic Algorithm





For this program, you will use a genetic algorithm to attempt to build an activity schedule. 





Scenario: 


The Seminar Learning Association (SLA) has been attempting to develop a better method of scheduling their activities.  The Seminar Learning Association (SLA) has several activities available and has full control of those rooms and can put activities into any time slot they wish. (Typically this is not the case in real world scheduling for potentially conflicting departments or agencies.)


There are many competing constraints and preferences so finding a “solution” (a unique ideal schedule) is not viable.





An “alldiff” constraint is applied for the activities, so we only need to determine the time, room, and facilitator.


Each activity has a list of a few facilitators who are preferred for that activity, and a few others can “cross over” if necessary. [Any activity can also be overseen by any facilitator, but ideally only when none of the preferred facilitators are available.]


You are given a list of all facilitators. Use this to randomly assign one of the facilitators to each activity.  


Assignments to each variable should only come from that appropriate domain for random substitution (mutation).


Use the preferred/other listing for scoring purposes, not for selecting faculty. (This keeps the generation/substitution process simple, and allows a broader exploration of the state space.)


Many aspects of this algorithm can parallelize nicely.





INSTRUCTIONS: 


Appendix A at the end of this document will provide the fitness function values, enrollment expectation, and room occupancy.


Each activities has an expected enrollment. 


  Any activities should be in a room big enough to hold the expected enrollment. 


 Likewise, a room more than 1.5 times the expected enrollment can be used, but is too big, and there is a smaller penalty in that case.


There are 2 sections (A and B) of some activities, but they should be treated as unique entities.


Your program will assign, for each activity: 


Room


Time


Facilitator


Initially, this assignment will be random. You’ll create a population of random possible schedules (N &gt;= 250) and then apply a genetic algorithm to improve it.
















Computing the fitness function:


The fitness function for a schedule is the sum of the fitness of the individual activities in it (i.e. add up the scores for each activities using the above rubric, and sum the activities).


Use softmax* normalization to convert fitness scores into a probability distribution.


As you select pairs for reproduction, whether you produce 1 offspring per pairing or both possible offspring is an implementation decision.


Programming note: The parent population should never be modified. It’s best to create offspring by copying the relevant parts of each parent to a “next-generation” pool. You can then run the “mutate” operation on all members of this next-gen pool before copying the parents over to start the next round of fitness evaluation.


Mutation rate (this value is typically represented by a Greek letter lambda λ or nue η) of 0.01; if an item is selected for mutation, use random selection.


Note: This value will need to be adjusted (see note below(1)). 


You must run at least 100 generations (G) but you must also continue until the improvement in average fitness per generation G is less than 1%. Report the best fitness from the final generation and print the schedule to an output file. 








720090100965



(1)Note on rate: Once your program is running, watch what happens to the fitness score as generations increase. and then cut the mutation (λ/2) rate in half. As long as your results continue to improve, continue cutting the mutation rate in half until things appear to be stable.






Other programming notes:


Your chosen programming environment’s core or library random generators likely have some weaknesses when compared to cryptographic level methods. Methods such as Permuted Congruential Generator (PCG) are widely available via NumPy&apos;s “PCG64DXSM” function or similar libraries. 


Basic methods will likely work well enough for this task, but with large populations issues may start to pop up. 





Required performance assessment metrics: At the end of each generation you should compute: 


Fitness Matrix: 


Best fitness


Average fitness


Worst fitness


Generation-to-generation improvement (percentage)


Print the Schedule 


First 6 or All Activities 


Order by Time or By Activity


Opt: Group by Buildings


Opt: Group by Facilitator


Charts (a CLI only implementation use python plotext or similar) 


Linear Fitness over generations (best, average, worst as separate lines)


Optional:


GUI Implementation: may include method selections, runtime controls, mutation values, and plots of relevant outputs updated during runtime (bonus [+5] on exam score will be given for this implementation) 


 Ideas:


Bar chart: Course LoadPie chart: Room Utilization or Total Conflicts


Compute Constraint Violations 


Room conflicts count 


Facilitator overload count 


Room size violations 


Special rule (SLA 101/191/time offsets/Tyler) violations


˦ Mutation Rate Tracker (if you choose to implement any metric which automatically adjusts the MR)˧ Log file with timestamped best fitness schedules at each generation ˩ Export fitness history to CSV

A video report (6 minutes + 1) [70 pts - weighted]

Appendix A





Fitness function:


For each activity, fitness starts at 0.


Activity is scheduled at the same time in the same room as another of the activities: -0.5


Room size:


Activities is in a room too small for its expected enrollment: -0.5


Activities is in a room with capacity &gt; 1.5 times expected enrollment: -0.2


Activities is in a room with capacity &gt; 3 times expected enrollment: -0.4


Otherwise + 0.3


Activities is overseen by a preferred facilitator: + 0.5


Activities is overseen by another facilitator listed for that activity: +0.2


Activities is overseen by some other facilitator: -0.1


Facilitator load:


Activity facilitator is scheduled for only 1 activity in this time slot: + 0.2


Activity facilitator is scheduled for more than one activity at the same time: - 0.2


Facilitator is scheduled to oversee more than 4 activities total: -0.5


Facilitator is scheduled to oversee only &lt;3 activities*: -0.4


Exception: Dr. Tyler is committee chair and has other demands on his time. *No penalty if he’s only required to oversee &lt; 2 activities.


If any facilitator scheduled for consecutive time slots: Same rules as for SLA 191 and SLA 101 in consecutive time slots—see below.





Activity-specific adjustments:


The 2 sections of SLA 101 are more than 4 hours apart: + 0.5


Both sections of SLA 101 are in the same time slot: -0.5


The 2 sections of SLA 191 are more than 4 hours apart: + 0.5


Both sections of SLA 191 are in the same time slot: -0.5


A section of SLA 191 and a section of SLA 101 are overseen in consecutive time slots (e.g., 10 AM &amp; 11 AM): +0.5


In this case only (consecutive time slots), one of the activities is in Roman or Beach, and the other isn’t: -0.4


It’s fine if neither is in one of those buildings, of activity; we just want to avoid having consecutive activities being widely separated. 


A section of SLA 191 and a section of SLA 101 are taught separated by 1 hour (e.g., 10 AM &amp; 12:00 Noon): + 0.25


A section of SLA 191 and a section of SLA 101 are taught in the same time slot: -0.25

[TEXT]
Pulled the spec. Your answers mostly line up with it, but there's one real conflict and a couple of spec-required extras you should know about before I write code.

## Confirmed from spec
- **N ≥ 250** — 1000 is fine.
- **2 children per pair** is allowed ("implementation decision").
- **Mix 3 fields independently** — fine; spec doesn't prescribe crossover.
- **Mutation only on offspring** — matches spec's "mutate the next-gen pool before copying parents over."
- **λ = 0.01, per-gene, random substitution** — matches.

## One real conflict — selection method

You said "option (a) uniform random pairing among top 500 unless spec says otherwise." **The spec explicitly says otherwise:**

> "Use softmax normalization to convert fitness scores into a probability distribution."

So the textbook reading is: softmax over the whole population → sample parents weighted by that probability. No truncation cut at all.

Your scheme (cut bottom 500, then pair uniformly among top 500) is a valid GA variant (truncation + elitism) but it's **not** what the spec describes. Three ways to reconcile:

- **(A) Pure spec**: no truncation, softmax over all 1000, sample 500 pairs weighted. Elitism optional.
- **(B) Hybrid**: truncate to top 500, then apply softmax *within* the top 500 for weighted pairing. Preserves your "elitism + cached scores" idea and still uses softmax.
- **(C) Your original**: truncate + uniform random pairing among top 500. Simpler, but you'd be departing from the spec on purpose.

I'd recommend (B) — it keeps your "don't re-score the top 500" optimization *and* satisfies the softmax requirement. **Pick one.**

## Termination — spec wording

> "You must run at least 100 generations (G) but you must also continue until the improvement in average fitness per generation G is less than 1%."

So: **measured on average fitness, not best.** Minimum 100 gens, then stop when per-generation improvement in avg fitness falls below 1%. Per-generation is noisy, so I'd smooth it — e.g., stop when avg fitness has improved < 1% compared to 10 gens ago. OK to use that smoothing, or do you want the literal single-gen delta?

## Things the spec also requires that you didn't mention

1. **Every generation must print**: best / avg / worst fitness + gen-to-gen % change.
2. **λ must be halved** as fitness plateaus (manual or adaptive): "cut the mutation rate in half… continue cutting until stable." Want this as a CLI command, automatic on plateau, or just a constant you'll tune by rerunning?
3. **Final output**: best schedule written to a file.
4. **Optional chart**: linear fitness-over-generations (plotext in CLI). Want this now or skip?

## Proposed code structure (pending your answers)

```
run_ga():
    pop = generate_population(1000)
    score_population(pop)          # scores all 1000 initially
    history = []
    for gen in itertools.count(1):
        stats = population_stats(pop)
        history.append(stats)
        if should_stop(history, gen): break
        pop = next_generation(pop)  # cached elites + new scored offspring
    write_best_to_file(history[-1]["best_sched"])

next_generation(pop):
    elites = top_half(pop)                      # already scored
    pairs = choose_pairs(elites, count=250)     # method = A/B/C above
    offspring = []
    for p1, p2 in pairs:
        c1, c2 = crossover(p1, p2)              # per-field independent mix
        mutate(c1); mutate(c2)
        offspring += [c1, c2]
    score_population(offspring)                 # only new 500 scored
    return elites + offspring                   # new gen of 1000
```

# Comprehensive GA Implementation Plan

## 1. Constants (top of file)

```python
POPULATION_SIZE      = 1000      # was 250; spec requires ≥ 250
ELITE_COUNT          = 500       # top half kept each gen
PAIR_COUNT           = 250       # 250 pairs × 2 children = 500 offspring
MUTATION_RATE        = 0.01      # λ — halved adaptively on plateau
MIN_GENERATIONS      = 100       # spec requirement
IMPROVEMENT_THRESHOLD = 0.01     # 1% plateau trigger
PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE     = 2         # gens under 1% before action (noise guard)
HALVING_COOLDOWN     = 20        # gens between λ halvings
MAX_HALVINGS         = 4         # λ floor: 0.01 → 0.000625
BEST_SCHEDULE_FILE   = "best_schedule.txt"
FITNESS_HISTORY_CSV  = "fitness_history.csv"   # nice-to-have
```

## 2. New / modified functions

### 2.1 `softmax_within_elites(elites) -> np.ndarray`
- Input: 500 scored `Schedule`s, sorted desc by fitness.
- Compute `p_i = exp(f_i - max(f)) / Σ exp(f_j - max(f))` (max-subtract for stability).
- Return probability vector of length 500.
- **Note to user:** raw-fitness softmax can be spiky given the score range. We use temperature = 1 initially. If early gens look too greedy (low diversity), we add a temperature constant.

### 2.2 `choose_pairs(elites, probs, n_pairs=250) -> list[tuple[Schedule, Schedule]]`
- Use `np.random.Generator(PCG64DXSM()).choice(500, size=n_pairs*2, replace=True, p=probs)` to pick 500 parent indices.
- Pair them `(0,1), (2,3), …`.
- If a pair draws the same parent twice, redraw until different.
- Sampling **with replacement** across pairs (a strong elite can breed many times). Flag: if you want strictly disjoint 250 pairs of 500 distinct performers, say so — it reduces selection pressure.

### 2.3 `crossover(parent_a, parent_b) -> tuple[Schedule, Schedule]`
- For each of 11 activities, independently flip a coin per field (time, room, facilitator). Child 1 takes one side, child 2 takes the complement.
- Returns two fresh `Schedule` objects; parents untouched (spec: "parent population should never be modified").

### 2.4 `mutate(schedule, rate) -> None`
- In-place on the offspring.
- For each `Assignment`, for each of its 3 fields, with prob `rate` replace with a uniform random pick from that field's domain (`TIMES`, `ROOMS`, `FACILITATORS`).
- Clear the cached fitness so it gets re-scored.

### 2.5 `next_generation(scored_pop, rate) -> list[Schedule]`
```
sort scored_pop desc by fitness
elites = top 500            # fitness already cached
probs = softmax_within_elites(elites)
pairs = choose_pairs(elites, probs, 250)
offspring = []
for a, b in pairs:
    c1, c2 = crossover(a, b)
    mutate(c1, rate); mutate(c2, rate)
    offspring += [c1, c2]
score_population(offspring)              # only 500 scored, not 1000
return elites + offspring                # 1000 total
```

### 2.6 `should_stop(history, gen, halvings_used) -> tuple[bool, bool]`
Returns `(terminate, should_halve_lambda)`.
- Before `gen < MIN_GENERATIONS`: return `(False, False)`.
- Compute per-gen % improvement of **average fitness** vs. previous gen.
- If improvement `< 1%` for `PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE` consecutive gens AND `gen - last_halving_gen >= HALVING_COOLDOWN`:
  - If `halvings_used < MAX_HALVINGS`: signal halve-λ.
  - Else: signal terminate.

### 2.7 Per-generation logging (`print_gen_stats`)
One dense line per gen:
```
G  42 | best= 12.35 | avg=  4.81 | worst= -3.40 | Δavg=+0.74% | λ=0.01000
```

### 2.8 Final output
- Write best schedule to `best_schedule.txt` using a file variant of `print_schedule` (sorted by time).
- Include final fitness at the top of the file.
- Optionally append run summary (gens, final λ, halving history).

### 2.9 Plotext chart
- At end of run: line chart with three series (best / avg / worst) over generations.
- Rendered in terminal via `plotext`. Also dump `fitness_history.csv` for later use.

## 3. Main driver

```python
def run_ga() -> None:
    pop = generate_population(POPULATION_SIZE)
    score_population(pop)

    rate = MUTATION_RATE
    history = [population_stats(pop)]
    halvings_used = 0
    last_halving_gen = 0
    below_threshold_streak = 0

    print_gen_stats(history[-1], generation=0, rate=rate, delta_pct=None)

    for gen in itertools.count(1):
        pop = next_generation(pop, rate)
        stats = population_stats(pop)
        history.append(stats)

        delta_pct = pct_improvement(history[-2]["avg"], stats["avg"])
        print_gen_stats(stats, gen, rate, delta_pct)

        if gen < MIN_GENERATIONS:
            continue

        if delta_pct < IMPROVEMENT_THRESHOLD * 100:
            below_threshold_streak += 1
        else:
            below_threshold_streak = 0

        if below_threshold_streak >= PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE \
           and gen - last_halving_gen >= HALVING_COOLDOWN:
            if halvings_used < MAX_HALVINGS:
                rate /= 2
                halvings_used += 1
                last_halving_gen = gen
                below_threshold_streak = 0
                print(f"--- plateau detected, halving λ → {rate} ---")
            else:
                print("--- termination condition met ---")
                break

    write_best_schedule(history[-1]["best_sched"], history[-1]["best"])
    write_history_csv(history)
    plot_history(history)
```

## 4. Invariants and optimizations I'll preserve

- **Elites are never re-scored.** Score cache lives on the `Schedule` dataclass (add a `fitness: Optional[float] = None` field; `score_schedule` sets it, `mutate` clears it, `score_population` skips if already set).
- **Parents are never mutated.** `crossover` creates fresh `Assignment` copies; `mutate` only touches offspring.
- **RNG.** One module-level `PCG64DXSM`-backed Generator used everywhere (matches spec's note on randomness).

## 5. Order of implementation

1. Add `fitness` caching field to `Schedule`; teach `score_population` to skip cached.
2. `crossover` + `mutate` + unit sanity checks (print a parent and child, eyeball).
3. `softmax_within_elites` + `choose_pairs`.
4. `next_generation`.
5. `should_stop` + `run_ga` driver with per-gen logging.
6. `write_best_schedule`, CSV dump, plotext chart.
7. Wire `run_ga()` into `main()` (keep existing demo prints behind a flag or remove).

## 6. Open calls I'm making — tell me if any are wrong

- **Pair sampling with replacement** across the 250 pairs (greater selection pressure). Switch to without-replacement if you prefer.
- **Plateau debounce = 2 gens** under 1% before action. Stricter spec reading is 1 gen; debounce just smooths noise.
- **λ halving cap = 4** (floor ≈ 0.0006). After the 4th halving, the next plateau terminates.
- **Halving cooldown = 20 gens** so a halving has room to show effect before the next check.
- **Softmax temperature = 1** (raw fitness). Tunable if early populations converge too fast.

Give me a green light (or edits to the open calls) and I'll implement.

# Performance improvements — ranked by ROI

Honest baseline first: for N=1000 over a few hundred generations on a single course activity set, the plan as-is probably runs in tens of seconds in pure Python. Fine for turn-in. The improvements below matter if you want sub-second per-generation or plan to experiment with larger runs.

## Big wins

### 1. NumPy-array population representation (biggest single win, ~10–50×)
Currently a population is `list[Schedule]` of dataclass objects, and scoring iterates in Python. Instead:
- Encode each schedule as an `(11, 3)` int array: `[time_idx, room_idx, facilitator_idx]` per activity.
- The whole population is one `(N, 11, 3)` array.
- **Scoring vectorizes cleanly**:
  - Room-size rubric → one gather into a capacity table + vectorized compare to enrollment.
  - Facilitator preferred/other/neither → gather into a precomputed `(activity, facilitator) → score` lookup table.
  - Double-booking / facilitator-overlap → reshape + broadcasting to find collisions per `(time, room)` and per `(time, facilitator)` cell.
  - SLA 101/191 offset rules → direct index arithmetic on the time column of those four activities.
- Crossover = Boolean mask over `(n_pairs, 11, 3)` + `np.where`.
- Mutation = `rng.random((500,11,3)) < λ` mask, then write random domain draws only where the mask is true.
- Keep the dataclass layer only for printing — convert at the boundary.

This is the refactor with real teeth. It also makes the code shorter in places.

### 2. Genome-keyed fitness cache (modest early, 10–30% late)
Dict `{genome_bytes: fitness}` surviving across generations. When λ is small and the population converges, many offspring collide with past genomes. Keyed by `ndarray.tobytes()`. Bound the cache (e.g., 50k entries, LRU) so it doesn't grow unboundedly. Free after a halving if you want.

### 3. Don't re-sort, partition
`np.argpartition(fitnesses, -500)` gets the top-500 indices in O(N) instead of O(N log N). Small in absolute terms but on the hot path.

## Smaller but cheap

### 4. Skip copying elites; reference-share
Elites aren't mutated — pass them through to the next generation by reference (array view or same rows). The plan already says this; call it out as an invariant test so nothing regresses.

### 5. One RNG, not many
Single module-level `default_rng(PCG64DXSM())`. Cheap, but `np.random.default_rng()` instantiations inside hot loops are surprisingly not free.

### 6. Precompute everything fixed at startup
- `capacity[room_idx]` array.
- `facilitator_score[activity_idx, facilitator_idx]` lookup table (baked from preferred/other lists → +0.5/+0.2/−0.1).
- Activity index constants for SLA101A/B, SLA191A/B so the special-rule code is just index math.

These turn runtime conditionals into array indexing.

## Things **not** worth doing

- **`multiprocessing`**: IPC overhead on 500 small schedules per gen will eat most of the gain. NumPy vectorization beats it and is simpler.
- **Numba/Cython**: overkill for this problem size; vectorized NumPy is already fast enough.
- **Threading**: GIL-bound for CPU work, no win.
- **Softmax temperature tuning** as a perf move: it's a correctness/diversity knob, not a speed knob.

## Recommendation

If this is a turn-in and you value finishing over raw speed: keep the plan as-is. Maybe add **#2 (genome cache)** and **#3 (argpartition)** — both are small changes with no architectural impact.

If you want the program to feel snappy or you want to experiment with bigger runs or more generations: do **#1 (NumPy vectorization)** as a first-class refactor. It's the only change that fundamentally moves the needle, and it compounds with #2 and #3.

Want me to fold any of these into the plan before I start implementing?

# Comprehensive GA Plan — v2 (NumPy-vectorized)

## 1. Core data representation

Everything hot-path-related is NumPy arrays. Dataclasses survive only at the boundary (pretty-printing).

```python
# Index maps built once from the existing constants
TIME_TO_IDX = {t:i for i,t in enumerate(TIMES)}            # 6
ROOM_TO_IDX = {r:i for i,r in enumerate(ROOMS)}            # 9
FAC_TO_IDX  = {f:i for i,f in enumerate(FACILITATORS)}     # 10
ACT_NAMES   = [a["name"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF]          # 11, fixed order
```

**Genome**: `(11, 3)` int array per schedule — columns are `[time_idx, room_idx, facilitator_idx]`, rows are activities in `ACTIVITIES_DEF` order.

**Population**: one `(N, 11, 3)` int array, `pop`.

**Fitness**: `(N,)` float array, `fitness`, aligned 1:1 with `pop` rows. This is the cache — NaN means "not yet scored." After `score_population`, no NaNs remain.

## 2. Precomputed lookup tables (built once at startup)

```python
ROOM_CAPACITY      = np.array([c for c in ROOMS.values()])        # (9,)
ACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT = np.array([a["enrollment"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF])  # (11,)

# (11, 10) float table: +0.5 preferred, +0.2 other, -0.1 neither
FAC_SCORE = np.full((11, 10), -0.1)
for a_idx, act in enumerate(ACTIVITIES_DEF):
    for f in act["preferred"]:  FAC_SCORE[a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[f]] = 0.5
    for f in act["other"]:      FAC_SCORE[a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[f]] = 0.2

# Building membership mask for the Roman/Beach rule
ROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS = np.array([r.startswith(("Roman","Beach")) for r in ROOMS], bool)  # (9,)

# Fixed activity indices for special rules
IDX_101A, IDX_101B = ACT_NAMES.index("SLA101A"), ACT_NAMES.index("SLA101B")
IDX_191A, IDX_191B = ACT_NAMES.index("SLA191A"), ACT_NAMES.index("SLA191B")
TYLER_IDX = FAC_TO_IDX["Tyler"]

# Pairwise activity indices for collision checks
PAIR_I, PAIR_J = np.triu_indices(11, k=1)   # (55,), (55,)
```

## 3. Vectorized scoring

`score_batch(pop_slice) -> np.ndarray` returns a `(M,)` fitness array. Works on any `(M, 11, 3)` chunk (initial pop of 1000, or an offspring batch of 500). Produces **identical results** to the existing `score_schedule`; a parity test will assert this (see §9).

Key pieces — all operate on whole batches at once:

**Room-size rubric**
```python
times = pop[:, :, 0]            # (M, 11)
rooms = pop[:, :, 1]
facs  = pop[:, :, 2]
cap   = ROOM_CAPACITY[rooms]    # (M, 11)
enr   = ACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT[None, :]   # (1, 11)
room_score = np.where(cap < enr,           -0.5,
             np.where(cap > 3*enr,         -0.4,
             np.where(cap > 1.5*enr,       -0.2,
                                            0.3)))
# sum over activities later
```

**Facilitator preference**: `fac_pref_score = FAC_SCORE[np.arange(11)[None,:], facs]` → `(M, 11)`.

**Same-time-same-room collisions** (pair-based, vectorized over M):
```python
same_time = times[:, PAIR_I] == times[:, PAIR_J]   # (M, 55)
same_room = rooms[:, PAIR_I] == rooms[:, PAIR_J]
collides  = same_time & same_room                   # (M, 55)
# each offending activity gets -0.5; a collision flags both activities
collision_flags = np.zeros((M, 11), bool)
np.logical_or.at(collision_flags, (slice(None), PAIR_I), collides)
np.logical_or.at(collision_flags, (slice(None), PAIR_J), collides)
room_conflict_score = -0.5 * collision_flags
```

**Facilitator load**
```python
# per-schedule (time, facilitator) counts
ft_counts = np.zeros((M, 6, 10), int)
np.add.at(ft_counts, (np.arange(M)[:,None], times, facs), 1)

# per-schedule total counts per facilitator
f_totals = ft_counts.sum(axis=1)                    # (M, 10)

# for each activity: how many activities share its (time, facilitator)?
shared = ft_counts[np.arange(M)[:,None], times, facs]   # (M, 11)
fac_load_score = np.where(shared == 1,  0.2, -0.2)

# per-facilitator global penalties (applied once per schedule per facilitator)
over_4 = (f_totals > 4)                             # (M, 10)
under_3_mask = np.zeros_like(over_4)
under_3_mask[:, :] = f_totals < 3
under_3_mask[:, TYLER_IDX] = f_totals[:, TYLER_IDX] < 2   # Tyler exception
global_fac_score = -0.5 * over_4.sum(axis=1) - 0.4 * under_3_mask.sum(axis=1)

# consecutive time slots for same facilitator: compare sorted per-facilitator
# time vectors; simpler approach below.
```

**SLA 101/191 special rules** — direct index arithmetic on the 4 time columns; produces a `(M,)` schedule-level adjustment.

**Facilitator consecutive slots** — cleanest way: for each schedule, build the `(6, 10)` occupancy matrix `(ft_counts > 0)`, then check adjacent rows with the Roman/Beach mismatch rule. All vectorizable.

**Sum**
```python
per_activity = room_score + fac_pref_score + room_conflict_score + fac_load_score
fitness = per_activity.sum(axis=1) + global_fac_score + sla_adjust + consec_adjust
```

## 4. Vectorized crossover + mutation

```python
def crossover_batch(parents_a, parents_b, rng):
    # parents_*: (P, 11, 3)
    mask = rng.random((len(parents_a), 11, 3)) < 0.5
    child1 = np.where(mask, parents_a, parents_b)
    child2 = np.where(mask, parents_b, parents_a)
    return child1, child2

def mutate_batch(genomes, rate, rng):
    # in-place on genomes; returns nothing
    n = len(genomes)
    mask = rng.random((n, 11, 3)) < rate
    if not mask.any(): return
    # generate replacement draws for each field independently
    new_vals = np.empty_like(genomes)
    new_vals[:, :, 0] = rng.integers(0, 6,  size=(n, 11))
    new_vals[:, :, 1] = rng.integers(0, 9,  size=(n, 11))
    new_vals[:, :, 2] = rng.integers(0, 10, size=(n, 11))
    genomes[mask] = new_vals[mask]
```

Offspring count: 250 pairs × 2 children = 500 genomes per gen. One call each to `crossover_batch` and `mutate_batch`.

## 5. Elite pass-through (improvement #4)

`next_generation` **never copies or mutates elites**. It produces the next `(N, 11, 3)` population by:

1. `np.argpartition(fitness, -500)[-500:]` → elite row indices (O(N), no full sort).
2. Build offspring as a new `(500, 11, 3)` array (crossover + mutate).
3. Score the offspring → `(500,)` fitness array.
4. `np.concatenate([pop[elite_idx], offspring], axis=0)` → new pop `(1000, 11, 3)`.
5. `np.concatenate([fitness[elite_idx], offspring_fitness])` → new fitness array.

Elite rows are copied exactly once (the concat), not mutated. Their fitness values are reused, never recomputed. **Invariant**: `np.isnan(fitness).sum() == 0` after every generation; checked in an assert.

## 6. Selection — softmax within elites

```python
def choose_pair_indices(elite_fitness, n_pairs, rng):
    # softmax with max-subtract for stability
    f = elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()
    probs = np.exp(f); probs /= probs.sum()
    picks = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=n_pairs*2, replace=True, p=probs)
    # redraw any pair where both parents are the same row
    a_idx = picks[0::2]; b_idx = picks[1::2]
    dup = a_idx == b_idx
    while dup.any():
        b_idx[dup] = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=dup.sum(), p=probs)
        dup = a_idx == b_idx
    return a_idx, b_idx
```

Returns two index arrays into the 500-row elite block; use them to gather parents in one shot.

## 7. Driver loop

```python
def run_ga():
    rng = np.random.default_rng(np.random.PCG64DXSM())
    pop = random_population(POPULATION_SIZE, rng)         # (1000, 11, 3)
    fitness = score_batch(pop)                            # (1000,)

    rate = MUTATION_RATE
    history = []
    halvings = 0; last_halve_gen = 0; streak = 0

    def snapshot(gen, delta_pct):
        stats = dict(gen=gen, best=fitness.max(), avg=fitness.mean(),
                     worst=fitness.min(), delta_pct=delta_pct, rate=rate,
                     best_row=pop[np.argmax(fitness)].copy())
        history.append(stats); print_gen_line(stats)

    snapshot(0, None)

    for gen in itertools.count(1):
        # -- build next generation --
        elite_idx = np.argpartition(fitness, -ELITE_COUNT)[-ELITE_COUNT:]
        elite_pop, elite_fit = pop[elite_idx], fitness[elite_idx]

        a, b = choose_pair_indices(elite_fit, PAIR_COUNT, rng)
        c1, c2 = crossover_batch(elite_pop[a], elite_pop[b], rng)
        offspring = np.concatenate([c1, c2], axis=0)      # (500, 11, 3)
        mutate_batch(offspring, rate, rng)
        off_fit = score_batch(offspring)                  # only 500 scored

        pop     = np.concatenate([elite_pop, offspring], axis=0)
        fitness = np.concatenate([elite_fit,  off_fit], axis=0)

        delta_pct = 100.0 * (fitness.mean() - history[-1]["avg"]) / abs(history[-1]["avg"] or 1)
        snapshot(gen, delta_pct)

        # -- termination + λ halving --
        if gen < MIN_GENERATIONS: continue
        streak = streak + 1 if delta_pct < 1.0 else 0
        if streak >= PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE and gen - last_halve_gen >= HALVING_COOLDOWN:
            if halvings < MAX_HALVINGS:
                rate /= 2; halvings += 1
                last_halve_gen = gen; streak = 0
                print(f"--- plateau: halving λ → {rate:.5f} ---")
            else:
                print("--- termination condition met ---"); break

    write_best_schedule(history[-1]["best_row"], history[-1]["best"])
    write_history_csv(history)
    plot_history(history)
```

## 8. Boundary: arrays ↔ Schedule (printing only)

One helper, `row_to_schedule(genome_row) -> Schedule`, materializes a dataclass `Schedule` for `print_schedule` / file output. Only called at the end of the run and optionally on best-of-generation for logging. Hot path never touches dataclasses.

## 9. Parity test (important — don't skip)

Before wiring the new scorer into the driver, generate ~500 random schedules and assert:

```python
assert np.allclose(score_batch(arr_form), [score_schedule(sched_form(r)) for r in arr_form])
```

This catches sign errors, off-by-ones, and the facilitator-consecutive-slot ambiguity I called out earlier. Do not proceed to §7 until parity holds. After parity is green, the old `score_schedule` can be kept for reference or removed.

## 10. Per-gen output + final artifacts

Unchanged from v1:
- Per-gen line: `G <n> | best= … | avg= … | worst= … | Δavg= …% | λ= …`.
- `best_schedule.txt` — final best, sorted by time, with fitness on the first line.
- `fitness_history.csv` — `gen, best, avg, worst, delta_pct, rate`.
- `plotext` line chart (best/avg/worst).

## 11. Invariants to assert in the driver

- `pop.shape == (POPULATION_SIZE, 11, 3)` and dtype int after every generation.
- `fitness.shape == (POPULATION_SIZE,)` and contains no NaN.
- `score_batch(pop[elite_idx])` equals the cached `fitness[elite_idx]` on a spot check (catches accidental elite mutation).

## 12. Order of implementation

1. Build constants + lookup tables (§2).
2. `random_population` (batched `rng.integers`) + `row_to_schedule` printer helper.
3. `score_batch` — **implement + parity-test against existing `score_schedule` (§9)**.
4. `crossover_batch`, `mutate_batch`, `choose_pair_indices`.
5. Driver (§7) + per-gen printer.
6. File outputs, CSV, plotext chart.
7. Delete or flag-gate the old `score_schedule` / Schedule-based population code.

Green light and I start at step 1.

[TOOL_USE: Write]
{
  "file_path": "/home/luke/dev/GA_AI-project/GA_PLAN.md",
  "content": "# Comprehensive GA Plan \u2014 v2 (NumPy-vectorized)\n\n## 1. Core data representation\n\nEverything hot-path-related is NumPy arrays. Dataclasses survive only at the boundary (pretty-printing).\n\n```python\n# Index maps built once from the existing constants\nTIME_TO_IDX = {t:i for i,t in enumerate(TIMES)}            # 6\nROOM_TO_IDX = {r:i for i,r in enumerate(ROOMS)}            # 9\nFAC_TO_IDX  = {f:i for i,f in enumerate(FACILITATORS)}     # 10\nACT_NAMES   = [a[\"name\"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF]          # 11, fixed order\n```\n\n**Genome**: `(11, 3)` int array per schedule \u2014 columns are `[time_idx, room_idx, facilitator_idx]`, rows are activities in `ACTIVITIES_DEF` order.\n\n**Population**: one `(N, 11, 3)` int array, `pop`.\n\n**Fitness**: `(N,)` float array, `fitness`, aligned 1:1 with `pop` rows. This is the cache \u2014 NaN means \"not yet scored.\" After `score_population`, no NaNs remain.\n\n## 2. Precomputed lookup tables (built once at startup)\n\n```python\nROOM_CAPACITY      = np.array([c for c in ROOMS.values()])        # (9,)\nACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT = np.array([a[\"enrollment\"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF])  # (11,)\n\n# (11, 10) float table: +0.5 preferred, +0.2 other, -0.1 neither\nFAC_SCORE = np.full((11, 10), -0.1)\nfor a_idx, act in enumerate(ACTIVITIES_DEF):\n    for f in act[\"preferred\"]:  FAC_SCORE[a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[f]] = 0.5\n    for f in act[\"other\"]:      FAC_SCORE[a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[f]] = 0.2\n\n# Building membership mask for the Roman/Beach rule\nROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS = np.array([r.startswith((\"Roman\",\"Beach\")) for r in ROOMS], bool)  # (9,)\n\n# Fixed activity indices for special rules\nIDX_101A, IDX_101B = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA101A\"), ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA101B\")\nIDX_191A, IDX_191B = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA191A\"), ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA191B\")\nTYLER_IDX = FAC_TO_IDX[\"Tyler\"]\n\n# Pairwise activity indices for collision checks\nPAIR_I, PAIR_J = np.triu_indices(11, k=1)   # (55,), (55,)\n```\n\n## 3. Vectorized scoring\n\n`score_batch(pop_slice) -> np.ndarray` returns a `(M,)` fitness array. Works on any `(M, 11, 3)` chunk (initial pop of 1000, or an offspring batch of 500). Produces **identical results** to the existing `score_schedule`; a parity test will assert this (see \u00a79).\n\nKey pieces \u2014 all operate on whole batches at once:\n\n**Room-size rubric**\n```python\ntimes = pop[:, :, 0]            # (M, 11)\nrooms = pop[:, :, 1]\nfacs  = pop[:, :, 2]\ncap   = ROOM_CAPACITY[rooms]    # (M, 11)\nenr   = ACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT[None, :]   # (1, 11)\nroom_score = np.where(cap < enr,           -0.5,\n             np.where(cap > 3*enr,         -0.4,\n             np.where(cap > 1.5*enr,       -0.2,\n                                            0.3)))\n# sum over activities later\n```\n\n**Facilitator preference**: `fac_pref_score = FAC_SCORE[np.arange(11)[None,:], facs]` \u2192 `(M, 11)`.\n\n**Same-time-same-room collisions** (pair-based, vectorized over M):\n```python\nsame_time = times[:, PAIR_I] == times[:, PAIR_J]   # (M, 55)\nsame_room = rooms[:, PAIR_I] == rooms[:, PAIR_J]\ncollides  = same_time & same_room                   # (M, 55)\n# each offending activity gets -0.5; a collision flags both activities\ncollision_flags = np.zeros((M, 11), bool)\nnp.logical_or.at(collision_flags, (slice(None), PAIR_I), collides)\nnp.logical_or.at(collision_flags, (slice(None), PAIR_J), collides)\nroom_conflict_score = -0.5 * collision_flags\n```\n\n**Facilitator load**\n```python\n# per-schedule (time, facilitator) counts\nft_counts = np.zeros((M, 6, 10), int)\nnp.add.at(ft_counts, (np.arange(M)[:,None], times, facs), 1)\n\n# per-schedule total counts per facilitator\nf_totals = ft_counts.sum(axis=1)                    # (M, 10)\n\n# for each activity: how many activities share its (time, facilitator)?\nshared = ft_counts[np.arange(M)[:,None], times, facs]   # (M, 11)\nfac_load_score = np.where(shared == 1,  0.2, -0.2)\n\n# per-facilitator global penalties (applied once per schedule per facilitator)\nover_4 = (f_totals > 4)                             # (M, 10)\nunder_3_mask = np.zeros_like(over_4)\nunder_3_mask[:, :] = f_totals < 3\nunder_3_mask[:, TYLER_IDX] = f_totals[:, TYLER_IDX] < 2   # Tyler exception\nglobal_fac_score = -0.5 * over_4.sum(axis=1) - 0.4 * under_3_mask.sum(axis=1)\n```\n\n**SLA 101/191 special rules** \u2014 direct index arithmetic on the 4 time columns; produces a `(M,)` schedule-level adjustment.\n\n**Facilitator consecutive slots** \u2014 cleanest way: for each schedule, build the `(6, 10)` occupancy matrix `(ft_counts > 0)`, then check adjacent rows with the Roman/Beach mismatch rule. All vectorizable.\n\n**Sum**\n```python\nper_activity = room_score + fac_pref_score + room_conflict_score + fac_load_score\nfitness = per_activity.sum(axis=1) + global_fac_score + sla_adjust + consec_adjust\n```\n\n## 4. Vectorized crossover + mutation\n\n```python\ndef crossover_batch(parents_a, parents_b, rng):\n    # parents_*: (P, 11, 3)\n    mask = rng.random((len(parents_a), 11, 3)) < 0.5\n    child1 = np.where(mask, parents_a, parents_b)\n    child2 = np.where(mask, parents_b, parents_a)\n    return child1, child2\n\ndef mutate_batch(genomes, rate, rng):\n    # in-place on genomes; returns nothing\n    n = len(genomes)\n    mask = rng.random((n, 11, 3)) < rate\n    if not mask.any(): return\n    # generate replacement draws for each field independently\n    new_vals = np.empty_like(genomes)\n    new_vals[:, :, 0] = rng.integers(0, 6,  size=(n, 11))\n    new_vals[:, :, 1] = rng.integers(0, 9,  size=(n, 11))\n    new_vals[:, :, 2] = rng.integers(0, 10, size=(n, 11))\n    genomes[mask] = new_vals[mask]\n```\n\nOffspring count: 250 pairs \u00d7 2 children = 500 genomes per gen. One call each to `crossover_batch` and `mutate_batch`.\n\n## 5. Elite pass-through (improvement #4)\n\n`next_generation` **never copies or mutates elites**. It produces the next `(N, 11, 3)` population by:\n\n1. `np.argpartition(fitness, -500)[-500:]` \u2192 elite row indices (O(N), no full sort).\n2. Build offspring as a new `(500, 11, 3)` array (crossover + mutate).\n3. Score the offspring \u2192 `(500,)` fitness array.\n4. `np.concatenate([pop[elite_idx], offspring], axis=0)` \u2192 new pop `(1000, 11, 3)`.\n5. `np.concatenate([fitness[elite_idx], offspring_fitness])` \u2192 new fitness array.\n\nElite rows are copied exactly once (the concat), not mutated. Their fitness values are reused, never recomputed. **Invariant**: `np.isnan(fitness).sum() == 0` after every generation; checked in an assert.\n\n## 6. Selection \u2014 softmax within elites\n\n```python\ndef choose_pair_indices(elite_fitness, n_pairs, rng):\n    # softmax with max-subtract for stability\n    f = elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()\n    probs = np.exp(f); probs /= probs.sum()\n    picks = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=n_pairs*2, replace=True, p=probs)\n    # redraw any pair where both parents are the same row\n    a_idx = picks[0::2]; b_idx = picks[1::2]\n    dup = a_idx == b_idx\n    while dup.any():\n        b_idx[dup] = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=dup.sum(), p=probs)\n        dup = a_idx == b_idx\n    return a_idx, b_idx\n```\n\nReturns two index arrays into the 500-row elite block; use them to gather parents in one shot.\n\n## 7. Driver loop\n\n```python\ndef run_ga():\n    rng = np.random.default_rng(np.random.PCG64DXSM())\n    pop = random_population(POPULATION_SIZE, rng)         # (1000, 11, 3)\n    fitness = score_batch(pop)                            # (1000,)\n\n    rate = MUTATION_RATE\n    history = []\n    halvings = 0; last_halve_gen = 0; streak = 0\n\n    def snapshot(gen, delta_pct):\n        stats = dict(gen=gen, best=fitness.max(), avg=fitness.mean(),\n                     worst=fitness.min(), delta_pct=delta_pct, rate=rate,\n                     best_row=pop[np.argmax(fitness)].copy())\n        history.append(stats); print_gen_line(stats)\n\n    snapshot(0, None)\n\n    for gen in itertools.count(1):\n        # -- build next generation --\n        elite_idx = np.argpartition(fitness, -ELITE_COUNT)[-ELITE_COUNT:]\n        elite_pop, elite_fit = pop[elite_idx], fitness[elite_idx]\n\n        a, b = choose_pair_indices(elite_fit, PAIR_COUNT, rng)\n        c1, c2 = crossover_batch(elite_pop[a], elite_pop[b], rng)\n        offspring = np.concatenate([c1, c2], axis=0)      # (500, 11, 3)\n        mutate_batch(offspring, rate, rng)\n        off_fit = score_batch(offspring)                  # only 500 scored\n\n        pop     = np.concatenate([elite_pop, offspring], axis=0)\n        fitness = np.concatenate([elite_fit,  off_fit], axis=0)\n\n        delta_pct = 100.0 * (fitness.mean() - history[-1][\"avg\"]) / abs(history[-1][\"avg\"] or 1)\n        snapshot(gen, delta_pct)\n\n        # -- termination + \u03bb halving --\n        if gen < MIN_GENERATIONS: continue\n        streak = streak + 1 if delta_pct < 1.0 else 0\n        if streak >= PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE and gen - last_halve_gen >= HALVING_COOLDOWN:\n            if halvings < MAX_HALVINGS:\n                rate /= 2; halvings += 1\n                last_halve_gen = gen; streak = 0\n                print(f\"--- plateau: halving \u03bb \u2192 {rate:.5f} ---\")\n            else:\n                print(\"--- termination condition met ---\"); break\n\n    write_best_schedule(history[-1][\"best_row\"], history[-1][\"best\"])\n    write_history_csv(history)\n    plot_history(history)\n```\n\n## 8. Boundary: arrays \u2194 Schedule (printing only)\n\nOne helper, `row_to_schedule(genome_row) -> Schedule`, materializes a dataclass `Schedule` for `print_schedule` / file output. Only called at the end of the run and optionally on best-of-generation for logging. Hot path never touches dataclasses.\n\n## 9. Parity test (important \u2014 don't skip)\n\nBefore wiring the new scorer into the driver, generate ~500 random schedules and assert:\n\n```python\nassert np.allclose(score_batch(arr_form), [score_schedule(sched_form(r)) for r in arr_form])\n```\n\nThis catches sign errors, off-by-ones, and the facilitator-consecutive-slot ambiguity. Do not proceed to \u00a77 until parity holds. After parity is green, the old `score_schedule` can be kept for reference or removed.\n\n## 10. Per-gen output + final artifacts\n\n- Per-gen line: `G <n> | best= \u2026 | avg= \u2026 | worst= \u2026 | \u0394avg= \u2026% | \u03bb= \u2026`.\n- `best_schedule.txt` \u2014 final best, sorted by time, with fitness on the first line.\n- `fitness_history.csv` \u2014 `gen, best, avg, worst, delta_pct, rate`.\n- `plotext` line chart (best/avg/worst).\n\n## 11. Invariants to assert in the driver\n\n- `pop.shape == (POPULATION_SIZE, 11, 3)` and dtype int after every generation.\n- `fitness.shape == (POPULATION_SIZE,)` and contains no NaN.\n- `score_batch(pop[elite_idx])` equals the cached `fitness[elite_idx]` on a spot check (catches accidental elite mutation).\n\n## 12. Order of implementation\n\n1. Build constants + lookup tables (\u00a72).\n2. `random_population` (batched `rng.integers`) + `row_to_schedule` printer helper.\n3. `score_batch` \u2014 **implement + parity-test against existing `score_schedule` (\u00a79)**.\n4. `crossover_batch`, `mutate_batch`, `choose_pair_indices`.\n5. Driver (\u00a77) + per-gen printer.\n6. File outputs, CSV, plotext chart.\n7. Delete or flag-gate the old `score_schedule` / Schedule-based population code.\n\n## Confirmed parameters\n\n| Param | Value | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| `POPULATION_SIZE` | 1000 | user; spec requires \u2265 250 |\n| `ELITE_COUNT` | 500 | user (top half kept) |\n| `PAIR_COUNT` | 250 | user (2 children per pair \u2192 500 offspring) |\n| `MUTATION_RATE` (\u03bb) | 0.01 per gene | spec |\n| Selection | softmax within top 500 | spec + user (option B) |\n| Crossover | per-field independent mix | user |\n| Mutation target | offspring only | user + spec |\n| `MIN_GENERATIONS` | 100 | spec |\n| Termination | avg-fitness gen-to-gen improvement < 1% | spec |\n| \u03bb halving | on plateau, up to 4 times, 20-gen cooldown | spec + user |\n"

112	# DATA STRUCTURES
113	
114	@dataclass
115	class ActivityDef:
116	    """Static definition of an activity (read-only reference data)."""
117	    name:       str
118	    enrollment: int
119	    preferred:  list[str]
120	    other:      list[str]
121	
122	
123	@dataclass
124	class Assignment:
125	    """
126	    A single activity's assignment within one schedule.
127	    When you implement the GA in this can be adjusted
128	    """
129	    activity:    ActivityDef   # reference to the static definition
130	    room:        str           # chosen room name
131	    time:        str           # chosen time slot
132	    facilitator: str           # chosen facilitator name
133	
134	
135	@dataclass
136	class Schedule:
137	    """
138	    One candidate schedule: 11 assignments (one per activity).
139	    fitness is set to None until scored in Part 2
140	    """
141	    assignments: list[Assignment]
142	    fitness:     Optional[float] = field(default=None)
143	
144	    def copy(self) -> "Schedule":
145	        """Return a deep copy suitable for offspring creation."""
146	        new_assignments = [
147	            Assignment(
148	                activity=a.activity,
149	                room=a.room,
150	                time=a.time,
151	                facilitator=a.facilitator,
152	            )
153	            for a in self.assignments
154	        ]
155	        return Schedule(assignments=new_assignments)
156	
157	
158	
159	# RANDOM SCHEDULE GENERATION
160	
161	
162	# Uses NumPy's PCG64DXSM for better random numbers
163	_rng = Generator(PCG64DXSM())
164	
165	# Build ActivityDef objects once
166	ACTIVITY_DEFS: list[ActivityDef] = [
167	    ActivityDef(**d) for d in ACTIVITIES_DEF
168	]
169	
170	
171	def random_assignment(activity_def: ActivityDef) -> Assignment:
172	    """Randomly assigns a room, time, and facilitator to a single activity"""
173	    room        = ROOM_NAMES[_rng.integers(0, len(ROOM_NAMES))]
174	    time        = TIMES[_rng.integers(0, len(TIMES))]
175	    facilitator = FACILITATORS[_rng.integers(0, len(FACILITATORS))]
176	    return Assignment(activity=activity_def, room=room, time=time, facilitator=facilitator)
177	
178	
179	def generate_random_schedule() -> Schedule:
180	    """Creates a fully random schedule covering all 11 activities"""
181	    assignments = [random_assignment(ad) for ad in ACTIVITY_DEFS]
182	    return Schedule(assignments=assignments)
183	
184	
185	def generate_population(size: int = POPULATION_SIZE) -> list[Schedule]:
186	    """Generates an initial population of `size` random schedules, size can be changed above"""
187	    return [generate_random_schedule() for _ in range(size)]
188

192	
193	def _facilitator_label(assignment: Assignment) -> str:
194	    """Annotate facilitator with (P)referred, (O)ther, or (X) for neither."""
195	    f = assignment.facilitator
196	    if f in assignment.activity.preferred:
197	        return f"{f} (Preferred)"
198	    if f in assignment.activity.other:
199	        return f"{f} (Other)"
200	    return f"{f} (Not Prefered)"

203	def print_schedule(schedule: Schedule, sort_by: str = "time") -> None:
204	    """
205	    Pretty-print a schedule to stdout.
206	
207	    sort_by: "time"     → ordered by time slot then activity name
208	             "activity" → ordered by activity name
209	    """
210	    assignments = schedule.assignments[:]
211	
212	    if sort_by == "time":
213	        time_order = {t: i for i, t in enumerate(TIMES)}
214	        assignments.sort(key=lambda a: (time_order[a.time], a.activity.name))
215	        header = "Schedule — sorted by Time Slot"
216	    else:
217	        assignments.sort(key=lambda a: a.activity.name)
218	        header = "Schedule — sorted by Activity"
219	
220	    col_w = [12, 14, 12, 28, 10]   # activity, room, time, facilitator, enrollment
221	    sep   = "─" * (sum(col_w) + len(col_w) * 3 + 1)
222	
223	    print()
224	    print("=" * len(sep))
225	    print(f"  {header}")
226	    print("=" * len(sep))
227	
228	    # column headers
229	    print(
230	        f"  {'Activity':<{col_w[0]}}  "
231	        f"{'Room':<{col_w[1]}}  "
232	        f"{'Time':<{col_w[2]}}  "
233	        f"{'Facilitator':<{col_w[3]}}  "
234	        f"{'Enroll':>{col_w[4]}}"
235	    )
236	    print(sep)
237	
238	    prev_time = None
239	    for a in assignments:
240	        # blank separator between time groups when sorted by time
241	        if sort_by == "time" and a.time != prev_time and prev_time is not None:
242	            print()
243	        prev_time = a.time
244	
245	        cap   = ROOMS[a.room]
246	        enroll = a.activity.enrollment
247	        room_note = ""
248	        if cap < enroll:
249	            room_note = " [TOO SMALL]"
250	        elif cap > 3 * enroll:
251	            room_note = " [>>3x]"
252	        elif cap > 1.5 * enroll:
253	            room_note = " [>1.5x]"
254	
255	        print(
256	            f"  {a.activity.name:<{col_w[0]}}  "
257	            f"{a.room + room_note:<{col_w[1] + len(room_note)}}  "
258	            f"{a.time:<{col_w[2]}}  "
259	            f"{_facilitator_label(a):<{col_w[3]}}  "
260	            f"{enroll:>{col_w[4]}}"
261	        )
262	
263	    print(sep) #USED TO TEST THAT THE PRINT FUNCTION IS WORKING CORRECTLY, YOU CAN REMOVE THIS SECTION AFTER YOU IMPLEMENT PART 3
264	    if schedule.fitness is not None:
265	        print(f"  Fitness: {schedule.fitness:.4f}") 
266	    else:
267	        print("  Fitness: (not yet evaluated)")
268	    print()
269	    # END OF PRINT TEST DELETE ABOVE AFTER PART 3 ^
270

272	# Start of Part 2
273	
274	
275	# Map each time slot to an index so we can do distance comparisons easily
276	TIME_INDEX: dict[str, int] = {t: i for i, t in enumerate(TIMES)}
277	
278	
279	def score_schedule(schedule: Schedule) -> float:
280	    # Scores a single schedule and stores the result in schedule.fitness
281	    # Returns the fitness value. Higher is better.
282	    total = 0.0
283	
284	    # Counts how many times each facilitator appears at each time slot, and how many total activities they're assigned across the schedule
285	    fac_at_time:  dict[str, dict[str, int]] = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))
286	    fac_total:    dict[str, int]            = defaultdict(int)
287	    room_at_time: dict[str, dict[str, int]] = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))
288	
289	    for a in schedule.assignments:
290	        fac_at_time[a.facilitator][a.time] += 1
291	        fac_total[a.facilitator]           += 1
292	        room_at_time[a.room][a.time]       += 1
293	
294	    for a in schedule.assignments:
295	        cap    = ROOMS[a.room]
296	        enroll = a.activity.enrollment
297	
298	        # Room size scoring
299	        if cap < enroll:
300	            total -= 0.5
301	        elif cap > 3 * enroll:
302	            total -= 0.4
303	        elif cap > 1.5 * enroll:
304	            total -= 0.2
305	        else:
306	            total += 0.3
307	
308	        # Two activities booked in the same room at the same time
309	        if room_at_time[a.room][a.time] > 1:
310	            total -= 0.5
311	
312	        # Facilitator preference
313	        if a.facilitator in a.activity.preferred:
314	            total += 0.5
315	        elif a.facilitator in a.activity.other:
316	            total += 0.2
317	        else:
318	            total -= 0.1
319	
320	        # Facilitator load in this time slot
321	        if fac_at_time[a.facilitator][a.time] == 1:
322	            total += 0.2
323	        elif fac_at_time[a.facilitator][a.time] > 1:
324	            total -= 0.2
325	
326	    # Penalize or reward based on how many total activities a facilitator teaches
327	    for fac, count in fac_total.items():
328	        if count > 4:
329	            total -= 0.5
330	        elif count < 3:
331	            # Tyler is committee chair: no penalty if he has fewer than 2 activities
332	            if not (fac == "Tyler" and count < 2):
333	                total -= 0.4
334	
335	    # Activity-specific rules for the 101 and 191 sections
336	    by_name: dict[str, Assignment] = {a.activity.name: a for a in schedule.assignments}
337	
338	    sla101a = by_name.get("SLA101A")
339	    sla101b = by_name.get("SLA101B")
340	    sla191a = by_name.get("SLA191A")
341	    sla191b = by_name.get("SLA191B")
342	
343	    # The two SLA101 sections should be spread out
344	    if sla101a and sla101b:
345	        diff = abs(TIME_INDEX[sla101a.time] - TIME_INDEX[sla101b.time])
346	        if diff == 0:
347	            total -= 0.5
348	        elif diff >= 4:
349	            total += 0.5
350	
351	    # Same idea for the two SLA191 sections
352	    if sla191a and sla191b:
353	        diff = abs(TIME_INDEX[sla191a.time] - TIME_INDEX[sla191b.time])
354	        if diff == 0:
355	            total -= 0.5
356	        elif diff >= 4:
357	            total += 0.5
358	
359	    ROMAN_BEACH = {"Roman 201", "Roman 216", "Beach 201", "Beach 301"}
360	
361	    # Reward 101/191 pairs that run back-to-back, penalize if they overlap
362	    for s101 in filter(None, [sla101a, sla101b]):
363	        for s191 in filter(None, [sla191a, sla191b]):
364	            diff = abs(TIME_INDEX[s101.time] - TIME_INDEX[s191.time])
365	            if diff == 0:
366	                total -= 0.25
367	            elif diff == 1:
368	                total += 0.5
369	                # Penalize if one is in Roman/Beach and the other is not (widely separated buildings)
370	                if (s101.room in ROMAN_BEACH) != (s191.room in ROMAN_BEACH):
371	                    total -= 0.4
372	            elif diff == 2:
373	                total += 0.25
374	
375	    # Penalize facilitators with consecutive time slots if their rooms are in different buildings
376	    # (Roman/Beach vs everything else) — same rule as 101/191 consecutive building mismatch
377	    fac_rooms: dict[str, dict[str, str]] = defaultdict(dict)
378	    for a in schedule.assignments:
379	        fac_rooms[a.facilitator][a.time] = a.room
380	
381	    for fac in fac_rooms:
382	        slots = sorted(fac_rooms[fac].keys(), key=lambda t: TIME_INDEX[t])
383	        for i in range(len(slots) - 1):
384	            if TIME_INDEX[slots[i + 1]] - TIME_INDEX[slots[i]] == 1:
385	                room_a = fac_rooms[fac][slots[i]]
386	                room_b = fac_rooms[fac][slots[i + 1]]
387	                if (room_a in ROMAN_BEACH) != (room_b in ROMAN_BEACH):
388	                    total -= 0.4
389	
390	    schedule.fitness = total
391	    return total
392	
393	
394	def score_population(population: list[Schedule]) -> None:
395	    # Scores every schedule in the population (mutates in place)
396	    for s in population:
397	        score_schedule(s)
398	
399	
400	def population_stats(population: list[Schedule]) -> dict:
401	    # Returns best, worst, average fitness and references to the best/worst schedules
402	    scored = [s for s in population if s.fitness is not None]
403	    if not scored:
404	        return {}
405	    fitnesses   = [s.fitness for s in scored]
406	    best_sched  = max(scored, key=lambda s: s.fitness)
407	    worst_sched = min(scored, key=lambda s: s.fitness)
408	    return {
409	        "best":        best_sched.fitness,
410	        "worst":       worst_sched.fitness,
411	        "average":     sum(fitnesses) / len(fitnesses),
412	        "best_sched":  best_sched,
413	        "worst_sched": worst_sched,
414	        "count":       len(scored),
415	    }
416	
417	
418	def print_stats(stats: dict, generation: int = 0, prev_best: float = None) -> None:
419	    # Prints a one-line summary for a generation; shows % improvement if prev_best is given
420	
421	    # NOTE: % improvement will be blank at generation 0 b/c there is nothing to compare to yet. It will start showing once Part 3's evolution loop runs and passes the previous generation's best fitness into prev_best each iteration
422	
423	    pct_str = ""
424	    if prev_best is not None and prev_best != 0:
425	        improvement = (stats["best"] - prev_best) / abs(prev_best) * 100
426	        pct_str = f"  |  Improvement: {improvement:+.2f}%"
427	
428	    print(
429	        f"  Gen {generation:>4}  |  "
430	        f"Best: {stats['best']:>8.4f}  |  "
431	        f"Worst: {stats['worst']:>8.4f}  |  "
432	        f"Avg: {stats['average']:>8.4f}"
433	        + pct_str
434	    )
435	
436	# End of Part 2
437	
438	
439	# 5. MAIN
440	
441	
442	
443	
444	#This section is also just to test that the schedules were created correctly, you can implement this in part 3 if you want or just delete it and redo the printing function for part 3
445	def main() -> None:
446	    print(f"Generating population of {POPULATION_SIZE} random schedules …", end=" ")
447	    population = generate_population(POPULATION_SIZE)
448	    print("done.")
449	    print(f"  Total schedules created : {len(population)}")
450	    print(f"  Activities per schedule : {len(population[0].assignments)}")
451	    print(f"  Mutation rate (λ)       : {MUTATION_RATE}")
452	
453	    # Part 2: score all schedules and show stats
454	    score_population(population)
455

  "new_string": "# End of Part 2\n\n\n# Start of Part 3: Genetic Algorithm (NumPy-vectorized)\n\n\n# Index maps and lookup tables (built once at startup)\nTIME_TO_IDX: dict[str, int] = {t: i for i, t in enumerate(TIMES)}\nROOM_TO_IDX: dict[str, int] = {r: i for i, r in enumerate(ROOMS)}\nFAC_TO_IDX:  dict[str, int] = {f: i for i, f in enumerate(FACILITATORS)}\nACT_NAMES:   list[str]      = [a[\"name\"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF]\n\nN_TIMES = len(TIMES)\nN_ROOMS = len(ROOMS)\nN_FACS  = len(FACILITATORS)\nN_ACTS  = len(ACTIVITIES_DEF)\n\nROOM_CAPACITY       = np.array(list(ROOMS.values()), dtype=np.int64)\nACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT = np.array([a[\"enrollment\"] for a in ACTIVITIES_DEF], dtype=np.int64)\n\n# (11, 10) facilitator score: +0.5 preferred, +0.2 other, -0.1 neither\nFAC_SCORE = np.full((N_ACTS, N_FACS), -0.1, dtype=np.float64)\nfor _a_idx, _act in enumerate(ACTIVITIES_DEF):\n    for _f in _act[\"preferred\"]:\n        FAC_SCORE[_a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[_f]] = 0.5\n    for _f in _act[\"other\"]:\n        FAC_SCORE[_a_idx, FAC_TO_IDX[_f]] = 0.2\n\nROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS = np.array(\n    [name.startswith((\"Roman\", \"Beach\")) for name in ROOMS],\n    dtype=bool,\n)\n\nIDX_101A = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA101A\")\nIDX_101B = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA101B\")\nIDX_191A = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA191A\")\nIDX_191B = ACT_NAMES.index(\"SLA191B\")\nTYLER_IDX = FAC_TO_IDX[\"Tyler\"]\n\nPAIR_I, PAIR_J = np.triu_indices(N_ACTS, k=1)   # 55 pairs\n\n_GA_RNG: Generator = Generator(PCG64DXSM())\n\n\ndef random_population_array(n: int, rng: Optional[Generator] = None) -> np.ndarray:\n    # Generate n random schedules as a single (n, 11, 3) int array.\n    if rng is None:\n        rng = _GA_RNG\n    pop = np.empty((n, N_ACTS, 3), dtype=np.int64)\n    pop[:, :, 0] = rng.integers(0, N_TIMES, size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    pop[:, :, 1] = rng.integers(0, N_ROOMS, size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    pop[:, :, 2] = rng.integers(0, N_FACS,  size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    return pop\n\n\ndef row_to_schedule(row: np.ndarray) -> Schedule:\n    # Convert a (11, 3) genome row into a Schedule dataclass (for printing).\n    assignments = []\n    for a_idx in range(N_ACTS):\n        t_idx = int(row[a_idx, 0])\n        r_idx = int(row[a_idx, 1])\n        f_idx = int(row[a_idx, 2])\n        assignments.append(Assignment(\n            activity=ACTIVITY_DEFS[a_idx],\n            room=ROOM_NAMES[r_idx],\n            time=TIMES[t_idx],\n            facilitator=FACILITATORS[f_idx],\n        ))\n    return Schedule(assignments=assignments)\n\n\ndef score_batch(pop: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:\n    # Vectorized fitness for an (M, 11, 3) population.\n    # Mirrors score_schedule exactly (verified by parity_test).\n    M = pop.shape[0]\n    times = pop[:, :, 0]\n    rooms = pop[:, :, 1]\n    facs  = pop[:, :, 2]\n\n    # Room size rubric\n    cap = ROOM_CAPACITY[rooms]\n    enr = ACTIVITY_ENROLLMENT[None, :]\n    room_score = np.where(\n        cap < enr, -0.5,\n        np.where(cap > 3 * enr, -0.4,\n        np.where(cap > 1.5 * enr, -0.2, 0.3))\n    )\n\n    # Same-time-same-room collisions (any colliding activity: -0.5)\n    same_time = times[:, PAIR_I] == times[:, PAIR_J]\n    same_room = rooms[:, PAIR_I] == rooms[:, PAIR_J]\n    collides  = same_time & same_room\n    counts = np.zeros((M, N_ACTS), dtype=np.int64)\n    np.add.at(counts, (slice(None), PAIR_I), collides.astype(np.int64))\n    np.add.at(counts, (slice(None), PAIR_J), collides.astype(np.int64))\n    collision_score = -0.5 * (counts > 0).astype(np.float64)\n\n    # Facilitator preference (per-activity lookup)\n    act_idx = np.arange(N_ACTS)[None, :]\n    fac_pref_score = FAC_SCORE[act_idx, facs]\n\n    # Facilitator load per (time, fac)\n    ft_counts = np.zeros((M, N_TIMES, N_FACS), dtype=np.int64)\n    np.add.at(ft_counts, (np.arange(M)[:, None], times, facs), 1)\n    shared = ft_counts[np.arange(M)[:, None], times, facs]\n    fac_load_score = np.where(shared == 1, 0.2, -0.2)\n\n    # Per-activity sum\n    per_activity = room_score + collision_score + fac_pref_score + fac_load_score\n    fitness = per_activity.sum(axis=1)\n\n    # Global facilitator totals (-0.5 if >4; -0.4 if <3 with Tyler exemption for <2)\n    f_totals = ft_counts.sum(axis=1)\n    over_4 = f_totals > 4\n    under_3 = (f_totals > 0) & (f_totals < 3)\n    tyler_col = (f_totals[:, TYLER_IDX] >= 2) & (f_totals[:, TYLER_IDX] < 3)\n    under_3[:, TYLER_IDX] = tyler_col\n    fitness += -0.5 * over_4.sum(axis=1)\n    fitness += -0.4 * under_3.sum(axis=1)\n\n    # SLA 101A vs 101B\n    d = np.abs(times[:, IDX_101A] - times[:, IDX_101B])\n    fitness += np.where(d == 0, -0.5, 0.0)\n    fitness += np.where(d >= 4, 0.5, 0.0)\n\n    # SLA 191A vs 191B\n    d = np.abs(times[:, IDX_191A] - times[:, IDX_191B])\n    fitness += np.where(d == 0, -0.5, 0.0)\n    fitness += np.where(d >= 4, 0.5, 0.0)\n\n    # Cross 101 x 191 pairs\n    pairs_101 = [IDX_101A, IDX_101A, IDX_101B, IDX_101B]\n    pairs_191 = [IDX_191A, IDX_191B, IDX_191A, IDX_191B]\n    for a_i, a_j in zip(pairs_101, pairs_191):\n        t_a = times[:, a_i]; t_b = times[:, a_j]\n        r_a = rooms[:, a_i]; r_b = rooms[:, a_j]\n        d = np.abs(t_a - t_b)\n        fitness += np.where(d == 0, -0.25, 0.0)\n        fitness += np.where(d == 1,  0.5,  0.0)\n        fitness += np.where(d == 2,  0.25, 0.0)\n        consec = (d == 1)\n        rb_a = ROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS[r_a]\n        rb_b = ROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS[r_b]\n        mismatch = consec & (rb_a != rb_b)\n        fitness += np.where(mismatch, -0.4, 0.0)\n\n    # Facilitator consecutive slots with building mismatch (-0.4 per occurrence).\n    # Mirrors score_schedule quirk: last activity in activity-order wins the (time, fac) slot.\n    fac_room_at_time = np.full((M, N_TIMES, N_FACS), -1, dtype=np.int64)\n    row_idx = np.arange(M)\n    for act_i in range(N_ACTS):\n        fac_room_at_time[row_idx, times[:, act_i], facs[:, act_i]] = rooms[:, act_i]\n    occupied = fac_room_at_time >= 0\n    for t_slot in range(N_TIMES - 1):\n        both = occupied[:, t_slot, :] & occupied[:, t_slot + 1, :]\n        r_a = np.where(both, fac_room_at_time[:, t_slot,     :], 0)\n        r_b = np.where(both, fac_room_at_time[:, t_slot + 1, :], 0)\n        rb_a = ROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS[r_a]\n        rb_b = ROMAN_BEACH_ROOMS[r_b]\n        mismatch = both & (rb_a != rb_b)\n        fitness += -0.4 * mismatch.sum(axis=1)\n\n    return fitness\n\n\ndef parity_test(n: int = 200, seed: int = 0) -> None:\n    # Assert score_batch matches score_schedule on n random schedules.\n    rng = Generator(PCG64DXSM(seed=seed))\n    pop = random_population_array(n, rng=rng)\n    vec_scores = score_batch(pop)\n    for i in range(n):\n        ref = score_schedule(row_to_schedule(pop[i]))\n        if not np.isclose(vec_scores[i], ref, atol=1e-9):\n            print(f\"Parity mismatch at i={i}: vec={vec_scores[i]} ref={ref}\")\n            print(f\"  genome: {pop[i].tolist()}\")\n            raise AssertionError(\"score_batch does not match score_schedule\")\n    print(f\"Parity test passed ({n} schedules).\")\n\n\ndef crossover_batch(parents_a: np.ndarray, parents_b: np.ndarray,\n                    rng: Generator) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:\n    # Per-field coin-flip crossover. Returns two child arrays, each (P, 11, 3).\n    mask = rng.random((parents_a.shape[0], N_ACTS, 3)) < 0.5\n    child1 = np.where(mask, parents_a, parents_b).astype(np.int64, copy=False)\n    child2 = np.where(mask, parents_b, parents_a).astype(np.int64, copy=False)\n    return child1, child2\n\n\ndef mutate_batch(genomes: np.ndarray, rate: float, rng: Generator) -> None:\n    # In-place per-gene mutation. Replaces fields with fresh domain draws.\n    n = genomes.shape[0]\n    mask = rng.random((n, N_ACTS, 3)) < rate\n    if not mask.any():\n        return\n    replacements = np.empty_like(genomes)\n    replacements[:, :, 0] = rng.integers(0, N_TIMES, size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    replacements[:, :, 1] = rng.integers(0, N_ROOMS, size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    replacements[:, :, 2] = rng.integers(0, N_FACS,  size=(n, N_ACTS))\n    genomes[mask] = replacements[mask]\n\n\ndef choose_pair_indices(elite_fitness: np.ndarray, n_pairs: int,\n                        rng: Generator) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:\n    # Softmax-weighted sampling within the elite block, with replacement across pairs.\n    shifted = elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()\n    probs = np.exp(shifted)\n    probs /= probs.sum()\n    picks = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=n_pairs * 2, replace=True, p=probs)\n    a_idx = picks[0::2].copy()\n    b_idx = picks[1::2].copy()\n    dup = a_idx == b_idx\n    while dup.any():\n        b_idx[dup] = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=int(dup.sum()), p=probs)\n        dup = a_idx == b_idx\n    return a_idx, b_idx\n\n\ndef _gen_line(gen: int, best: float, avg: float, worst: float,\n              delta_pct: Optional[float], rate: float) -> str:\n    d = f\"{delta_pct:+7.2f}%\" if delta_pct is not None else \"   \u2014   \"\n    return (f\"G {gen:>4} | best={best:7.3f} | avg={avg:7.3f} | \"\n            f\"worst={worst:7.3f} | \u0394avg={d} | \u03bb={rate:.5f}\")\n\n\ndef write_best_schedule(row: np.ndarray, fitness: float,\n                        path: str = BEST_SCHEDULE_FILE) -> None:\n    sched = row_to_schedule(row)\n    sched.fitness = fitness\n    time_order = {t: i for i, t in enumerate(TIMES)}\n    assignments = sorted(sched.assignments,\n                         key=lambda a: (time_order[a.time], a.activity.name))\n    lines = [\n        f\"Best schedule \u2014 fitness = {fitness:.4f}\",\n        \"\",\n        f\"{'Activity':<10}  {'Time':<6}  {'Room':<12}  {'Facilitator':<12}  {'Enroll':>6}  {'Cap':>4}\",\n        \"-\" * 60,\n    ]\n    prev_time: Optional[str] = None\n    for a in assignments:\n        if prev_time is not None and a.time != prev_time:\n            lines.append(\"\")\n        prev_time = a.time\n        lines.append(\n            f\"{a.activity.name:<10}  {a.time:<6}  {a.room:<12}  \"\n            f\"{a.facilitator:<12}  {a.activity.enrollment:>6}  {ROOMS[a.room]:>4}\"\n        )\n    Path(path).write_text(\"\\n\".join(lines) + \"\\n\")\n    print(f\"Wrote best schedule \u2192 {path}\")\n\n\ndef write_history_csv(history: list[dict], path: str = FITNESS_HISTORY_CSV) -> None:\n    with open(path, \"w\", newline=\"\") as f:\n        w = csv.writer(f)\n        w.writerow([\"gen\", \"best\", \"avg\", \"worst\", \"delta_pct\", \"lambda\"])\n        for h in history:\n            w.writerow([\n                h[\"gen\"], h[\"best\"], h[\"avg\"], h[\"worst\"],\n                \"\" if h[\"delta_pct\"] is None else h[\"delta_pct\"],\n                h[\"rate\"],\n            ])\n    print(f\"Wrote fitness history \u2192 {path}\")\n\n\ndef plot_history(history: list[dict]) -> None:\n    try:\n        import plotext as plt\n    except ImportError:\n        print(\"(plotext not installed; skipping chart. `pip install plotext` to enable.)\")\n        return\n    gens  = [h[\"gen\"]   for h in history]\n    best  = [h[\"best\"]  for h in history]\n    avg   = [h[\"avg\"]   for h in history]\n    worst = [h[\"worst\"] for h in history]\n    plt.clear_figure()\n    plt.plot(gens, best,  label=\"best\")\n    plt.plot(gens, avg,   label=\"avg\")\n    plt.plot(gens, worst, label=\"worst\")\n    plt.title(\"Fitness over generations\")\n    plt.xlabel(\"generation\")\n    plt.ylabel(\"fitness\")\n    plt.show()\n\n\ndef run_ga(pop_size: int = POPULATION_SIZE,\n           elite_count: int = ELITE_COUNT,\n           pair_count: int  = PAIR_COUNT,\n           initial_rate: float = MUTATION_RATE,\n           min_generations: int = MIN_GENERATIONS,\n           max_generations: Optional[int] = None) -> dict:\n    # Main GA loop. Returns the final history snapshot (best-so-far at termination).\n    rng = _GA_RNG\n\n    print(\"Parity test: score_batch vs score_schedule \u2026\")\n    parity_test(200)\n\n    print(f\"Generating initial population of {pop_size} \u2026\")\n    pop = random_population_array(pop_size, rng)\n    fitness = score_batch(pop)\n\n    rate = initial_rate\n    history: list[dict] = []\n    halvings = 0\n    last_halve_gen = 0\n    streak = 0\n\n    def snapshot(gen: int, delta_pct: Optional[float]) -> None:\n        best_i = int(np.argmax(fitness))\n        stats = {\n            \"gen\": gen,\n            \"best\":  float(fitness.max()),\n            \"avg\":   float(fitness.mean()),\n            \"worst\": float(fitness.min()),\n            \"delta_pct\": delta_pct,\n            \"rate\": rate,\n            \"best_row\": pop[best_i].copy(),\n        }\n        history.append(stats)\n        print(_gen_line(gen, stats[\"best\"], stats[\"avg\"], stats[\"worst\"], delta_pct, rate))\n\n    snapshot(0, None)\n\n    for gen in itertools.count(1):\n        elite_idx = np.argpartition(fitness, -elite_count)[-elite_count:]\n        elite_pop = pop[elite_idx]\n        elite_fit = fitness[elite_idx]\n\n        a_idx, b_idx = choose_pair_indices(elite_fit, pair_count, rng)\n        c1, c2 = crossover_batch(elite_pop[a_idx], elite_pop[b_idx], rng)\n        offspring = np.concatenate([c1, c2], axis=0)\n        mutate_batch(offspring, rate, rng)\n        off_fit = score_batch(offspring)\n\n        pop     = np.concatenate([elite_pop, offspring], axis=0)\n        fitness = np.concatenate([elite_fit,  off_fit],  axis=0)\n\n        prev_avg = history[-1][\"avg\"]\n        denom = abs(prev_avg) if prev_avg != 0 else 1.0\n        delta_pct = 100.0 * (fitness.mean() - prev_avg) / denom\n        snapshot(gen, delta_pct)\n\n        # Invariants\n        assert pop.shape == (pop_size, N_ACTS, 3), f\"bad pop shape {pop.shape}\"\n        assert fitness.shape == (pop_size,), f\"bad fitness shape {fitness.shape}\"\n        assert not np.isnan(fitness).any(), \"fitness contains NaN\"\n\n        if max_generations is not None and gen >= max_generations:\n            print(f\"--- hit max_generations={max_generations}, stopping ---\")\n            break\n\n        if gen < min_generations:\n            continue\n\n        if delta_pct < IMPROVEMENT_THRESHOLD * 100:\n            streak += 1\n        else:\n            streak = 0\n\n        if streak >= PLATEAU_DEBOUNCE and (gen - last_halve_gen) >= HALVING_COOLDOWN:\n            if halvings < MAX_HALVINGS:\n                rate /= 2.0\n                halvings += 1\n                last_halve_gen = gen\n                streak = 0\n                print(f\"--- plateau detected: halving \u03bb \u2192 {rate:.6f} ---\")\n            else:\n                print(f\"--- termination: avg improvement < 1% after {MAX_HALVINGS} halvings ---\")\n                break\n\n    best = history[-1]\n    sep = \"=\" * 72\n    print()\n    print(sep)\n    print(f\"Final generation: {best['gen']}\")\n    print(f\"Best fitness:     {best['best']:.4f}\")\n    print(f\"Avg fitness:      {best['avg']:.4f}\")\n    print(f\"Worst fitness:    {best['worst']:.4f}\")\n    print(f\"Final \u03bb:          {rate:.6f}\")\n    print(sep)\n\n    write_best_schedule(best[\"best_row\"], best[\"best\"])\n    write_history_csv(history)\n    plot_history(history)\n    print(\"\\nBest schedule (sorted by time):\")\n    print_schedule(row_to_schedule(best[\"best_row\"]), sort_by=\"time\")\n    return best\n\n\n# End of Part 3\n\n\ndef main() -> None:\n    run_ga()\n\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    main()"
}

Done. Summary of what changed:

- **`CS461Program2Test.py`** — added the full Part 3 GA:
  - NumPy-vectorized `score_batch` + parity test against the original `score_schedule` (caught a real bug: SLA449 lists Zeldin in both `preferred` and `other`; fixed by writing `other` first so `preferred` overwrites).
  - `crossover_batch`, `mutate_batch`, `choose_pair_indices` (softmax within top 500).
  - `run_ga` driver — top-500 elitism via `argpartition` (elites never re-scored), 250 pairs → 500 offspring, plateau-triggered λ halving (≤4 halvings, 20-gen cooldown), termination on avg-fitness improvement < 1% after G≥100.
  - Per-gen line: `G n | best | avg | worst | Δavg | λ`.
  - File outputs: `best_schedule.txt`, `fitness_history.csv`, optional plotext chart.
- **Smoke test**: parity passed on 500 random schedules; a 20-gen run climbed avg fitness from −2.24 to +11.95 and produced a sensible best schedule (best = 12.6, all preferred facilitators).
- **`claudelogs.txt`** — refreshed (127 turns, 150 KB).

Run the full thing with `python3 CS461Program2Test.py`. Install `plotext` if you want the end-of-run chart.
