## Fitness / GA loop
| # | Spec line | Code | |
|---|---|---|---|
| 16 | Fitness = sum of per-activity fitness | `score_schedule` sums per-activity then adds schedule-level rules | ✓ |
| 17 | Use softmax normalization for selection | `choose_pair_indices` [L671-687](CS461Program2Test.py#L671-L687) — tempered softmax (T=2.0) | ✓* |
| 18 | 1 or 2 offspring per pairing (your choice) | Produces both (c1, c2) | ✓ |
| 19 | **Parent population never modified** | `elite_pop` is fancy-indexed copy; `crossover_batch` returns new arrays via `np.where`; mutation runs on offspring only | ✓ |
| 20 | Copy parent parts into next-gen pool, then mutate pool, then parents join next round | Offspring pool built via crossover, mutated in place [L922-924](CS461Program2Test.py#L922-L924), then elites rejoin via concat [L927](CS461Program2Test.py#L927) | ✓ |
| 21 | Mutation rate λ = 0.01 | `MUTATION_RATE = 0.01` [L117](CS461Program2Test.py#L117) | ✓ |
| 22 | On mutation, use random selection from domain | `mutate_batch` picks fresh uniform draws | ✓ |
| 23 | Run at least 100 generations | `MIN_GENERATIONS = 100` [L119](CS461Program2Test.py#L119); enforced at [L946-947](CS461Program2Test.py#L946-L947) | ✓ |
| 24 | Continue until avg-fitness improvement < 1% | `IMPROVEMENT_THRESHOLD = 0.01` checked against `delta_pct` on avg [L932, L949](CS461Program2Test.py#L932) | ✓ |
| 25 | Report best fitness from final generation | Printed at [L973](CS461Program2Test.py#L973) | ✓ |
| 26 | Print the schedule to an output file | `write_best_schedule` → `best_schedule.txt` | ✓ |
| 27 | Halve λ on plateau; continue halving until stable | `rate /= 2.0` [L956](CS461Program2Test.py#L956), capped by `MAX_HALVINGS = 4` | ✓ |

\* *Tempered softmax (dividing by T=2 before exp) is still softmax; T is a selection-pressure knob. The spec's `*` after "softmax" is ambiguous about whether temperature is allowed — defensible.*

## Appendix A — Fitness rules
| # | Rule | Value | Code | |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 50 | Same time & same room as another activity | −0.5 | Collision check [L325-326, L544-551](CS461Program2Test.py#L325-L326) | ✓ |
| 51 | Room too small | −0.5 | [L315-316](CS461Program2Test.py#L315-L316) | ✓ |
| 52 | Room cap > 1.5× enrollment | −0.2 | [L319-320](CS461Program2Test.py#L319-L320) | ✓ |
| 53 | Room cap > 3× enrollment | −0.4 | [L317-318](CS461Program2Test.py#L317-L318) — checked **before** the 1.5× branch so 3× takes precedence | ✓ |

Two separate spec quirks. Let me explain each.

## #73 — "7 Rooms" vs 9 rooms

The spec contains a self-contradiction:

**One sentence** (in the "Selections consist of" line):
> "Selections consist of: 11 Activities, **7 Rooms**, and 6 Times"

**Then the room table** that immediately follows lists **9 rooms**:
```
Beach 201   18
Beach 301   25
Frank 119   95
Loft 206    55
Loft 310    48
James 325  110
Roman 201   40
Roman 216   80
Slater 003  32
```

Count them — that's 9, not 7. The "7 Rooms" number in the prose doesn't match the authoritative room table. This is almost certainly a typo in the spec (likely copy-pasted from an older version with fewer rooms).

**Your code uses all 9** from the table. That's the correct call because:
- The fitness function needs per-room capacities, which only exist in the table
- You'd have to arbitrarily drop 2 rooms with no guidance on which ones
- The room table is clearly the authoritative data source

**Recommendation for your video:** mention it briefly — *"the spec says 7 rooms in one place but lists 9 in the table; I went with the table since that's where the capacities are defined."* That signals to the grader you caught the inconsistency rather than ignored it.

## The softmax asterisk

The spec writes:
> "Use softmax\* normalization to convert fitness scores into a probability distribution."

The asterisk (`*`) is suspicious — usually it marks a footnote, but **there's no corresponding footnote anywhere in the document**. (I re-checked the extracted text — the only real footnote marker is `(1)` for the mutation-rate note.) So `softmax*` is likely meant to signal "softmax-like / softmax-family" rather than strict textbook softmax.

### Strict softmax vs. what your code does

Textbook softmax over fitnesses $f_1..f_n$:

$$p_i = \frac{e^{f_i}}{\sum_j e^{f_j}}$$

Your code at [CS461Program2Test.py:671-687](CS461Program2Test.py#L671-L687):

```python
shifted = (elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()) / max(temperature, 1e-9)
probs = np.exp(shifted)
probs /= probs.sum()
```

Two things going on:

**1. Max-subtraction** — `elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()`
This is numerical-stability boilerplate, not a semantic change. It produces the **exact same probabilities** as plain softmax (shifting all inputs by a constant cancels out in the ratio). Without it, `np.exp(large_fitness)` can overflow to `inf`. Every softmax implementation does this.

**2. Temperature scaling** — `/ max(temperature, 1e-9)` with `SELECTION_TEMPERATURE = 2.0`
This one is a real algorithmic choice. The formula becomes:

$$p_i = \frac{e^{f_i / T}}{\sum_j e^{f_j / T}}$$

- **T = 1**: plain softmax (greedy-ish; a fitness 1 point higher gets ~2.7× the probability)
- **T = 2** (your code): flattens the distribution, giving less-fit elites more chance of being picked
- **T → ∞**: uniform selection
- **T → 0**: argmax selection

Why flatten? Without temperature, once the elite pool's fitness spread is a few points wide, the top schedule dominates selection and you lose diversity — the GA collapses onto one genome and stops exploring. T=2 keeps selection pressure sensible.

### Is temperature a spec violation?

- **Strict reading:** spec says "softmax", your code does "softmax with temperature", therefore it's not pure softmax.
- **Practical reading:** tempered softmax *is* softmax applied to scaled inputs; it's still in the softmax family. The asterisk after "softmax\*" arguably acknowledges variants.
- **Pedagogical reading:** GA courses commonly teach temperature as part of softmax selection.

My read: **fine, but worth a line in the video.** Something like *"I used softmax with a temperature of 2.0 so one dominant elite doesn't monopolize breeding — without it the population collapses within ~20 generations."*

If you want to be maximally conservative and match strict softmax, set `SELECTION_TEMPERATURE = 1.0` at [CS461Program2Test.py:118](CS461Program2Test.py#L118). The code will still work — you'll likely just converge faster and to slightly worse optima.

Want me to change it to T=1 for strict compliance, or leave T=2 and you'll defend it in the video?

[TEXT]
Let me explain the effect, then actually run both settings to show concretely.

## Theory

With fitnesses $f_1..f_n$ and temperature $T$, probability of picking elite $i$ is:

$$p_i = \frac{e^{f_i/T}}{\sum_j e^{f_j/T}}$$

A 1-point fitness gap between two elites translates to:

| T | Prob ratio (1-pt gap) | Prob ratio (3-pt gap) |
|---|---|---|
| **1** (plain softmax) | $e^1 ≈ 2.7$× | $e^3 ≈ 20$× |
| **2** (current) | $e^{0.5} ≈ 1.65$× | $e^{1.5} ≈ 4.5$× |
| 5 | $e^{0.2} ≈ 1.2$× | $e^{0.6} ≈ 1.8$× |

Late in the run, the elite block's fitness spread is usually 3–6 points. At T=1 that means the **top 5–10 elites dominate breeding almost entirely** — the other 90+ elites are nearly invisible.

Predicted consequences of removing temperature (T=1):
- **Faster initial convergence** — selection pressure is higher, so average fitness climbs quicker
- **Earlier plateau / lower ceiling** — genetic diversity collapses faster; offspring start inbreeding from a narrow slice
- **More variance across seeds** — some seeds get lucky and find good optima; others get stuck

Let me run both and show real numbers.

## Turn 454 — ASSISTANT — 2026-04-21T17:41:32.671Z

[TOOL_USE: Bash]
{
  "command": "python3 << 'EOF'\nimport sys, time\nimport numpy as np\nsys.path.insert(0, '.')\nimport CS461Program2Test as ga\n\n_orig_choose = ga.choose_pair_indices\n\ndef make_chooser(T):\n    def chooser(elite_fitness, n_pairs, rng, temperature=T):\n        shifted = (elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()) / max(T, 1e-9)\n        probs = np.exp(shifted); probs /= probs.sum()\n        picks = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=n_pairs*2, replace=True, p=probs)\n        a = picks[0::2].copy(); b = picks[1::2].copy()\n        dup = a == b\n        while dup.any():\n            b[dup] = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=int(dup.sum()), p=probs)\n            dup = a == b\n        return a, b\n    return chooser\n\ndef run_batch(T, seeds, max_gen=180):\n    ga.choose_pair_indices = make_chooser(T)\n    results = []\n    for s in seeds:\n        t0 = time.time()\n        r = ga.run_ga(seed=s, verbose=False, max_generations=max_gen, write_outputs=False)\n        results.append({\"seed\": s, \"best\": r[\"best\"], \"avg\": r[\"avg\"], \"gen\": r[\"gen\"],\n                        \"halvings\": len(r[\"halving_gens\"]), \"elapsed\": time.time()-t0})\n    return results\n\nseeds = [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7]\nprint(\"Running T=1 \u2026\"); r1 = run_batch(1.0, seeds)\nprint(\"Running T=2 \u2026\"); r2 = run_batch(2.0, seeds)\nprint(\"Running T=5 \u2026\"); r5 = run_batch(5.0, seeds)\n\ndef summary(tag, rs):\n    bests = np.array([r[\"best\"] for r in rs])\n    avgs  = np.array([r[\"avg\"]  for r in rs])\n    print()\n    print(tag)\n    print(f\"  per-seed best : [\" + \", \".join(f\"{b:.2f}\" for b in bests) + \"]\")\n    print(f\"  best  mean={bests.mean():.3f}  std={bests.std():.3f}  min={bests.min():.2f}  max={bests.max():.2f}\")\n    print(f\"  pop avg at stop mean={avgs.mean():.3f}\")\n\nsummary(\"T=1 (plain softmax, no temperature)\", r1)\nsummary(\"T=2 (current)\",                        r2)\nsummary(\"T=5 (flatter)\",                        r5)\nEOF",

probs /= probs.sum()\n        picks = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=n_pairs*2, replace=True, p=probs)\n        a = picks[0::2].copy(); b = picks[1::2].copy()\n        dup = a == b\n        while dup.any():\n            b[dup] = rng.choice(len(elite_fitness), size=int(dup.sum()), p=probs)\n            dup = a == b\n        return a, b\n    return chooser\n\ndef run_and_snapshot(T, seeds, snapshot_gens=(10, 30, 60, 100, 150)):\n    ga.choose_pair_indices = make_chooser(T)\n    per_gen_best = {g: [] for g in snapshot_gens}\n    per_gen_avg  = {g: [] for g in snapshot_gens}\n    per_gen_div  = {g: [] for g in snapshot_gens}   # std across pop (diversity proxy)\n    for s in seeds:\n        r = ga.run_ga(seed=s, verbose=False, max_generations=max(snapshot_gens), write_outputs=False)\n        for g in snapshot_gens:\n            h = r[\"history\"][g]\n            per_gen_best[g].append(h[\"best\"])\n            per_gen_avg[g].append(h[\"avg\"])\n            per_gen_div[g].append(h[\"best\"] - h[\"avg\"])  # spread = diversity proxy\n    return per_gen_best, per_gen_avg, per_gen_div\n\nseeds = list(range(10))\nsnaps = (10, 30, 60, 100, 150)\n\ndata = {}\nfor T in [1.0, 2.0, 5.0]:\n    print(f\"Running T={T} \u2026\")\n    data[T] = run_and_snapshot(T, seeds, snaps)\n\nprint()\nprint(f\"{'T':>4} {'gen':>5} | {'best mean':>10} {'best std':>9} | {'avg mean':>10} | {'best\u2212avg':>9}\")\nprint(\"-\" * 60)\nfor T in [1.0, 2.0, 5.0]:\n    per_gen_best, per_gen_avg, per_gen_div = data[T]\n    for g in snaps:\n        bm = np.mean(per_gen_best[g]); ## Turn 461 — ASSISTANT — 2026-04-21T17:43:35.550Z

[TEXT]
**In practice, almost no effect on final fitness.** Here's the real picture:

| T | Gen 10 best | Gen 10 spread (best−avg) | Gen 30 best | Final best (gen 150) |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **1** (plain) | 12.52 | **1.03** | 12.78 | 12.79 |
| **2** (current) | 12.28 | 1.81 | 12.78 | 12.78 |
| **5** (flat) | 12.40 | 2.33 | 12.77 | 12.80 |

### What actually changes

1. **Early convergence speed** — at gen 10, T=1 is already at 12.52 while T=2 is at 12.28. Plain softmax exploits the top elite more aggressively, so initial climb is steeper.

2. **Population diversity** — the `best−avg` column is a diversity proxy. At gen 10, T=1 has spread of **1.03** vs T=2's **1.81** — plain softmax has collapsed the population onto the top performer roughly twice as fast.

3. **Final fitness** — essentially identical across all three (12.78–12.80). Standard deviation across 10 seeds is also the same (~0.18). No T setting gets stuck in worse optima on this problem.

### Why doesn't temperature matter more?

- **Big elite pool (100)** — even greedy selection still has enough distinct parents to avoid total inbreeding
- **1% mutation** — constantly injects fresh genetic material
- **Halving schedule** — the cooling regimen drives everyone to convergence regardless
- **Fitness ceiling ~13.0** — the problem has a natural ceiling, so early vs late convergence all hit the same wall

### Recommendation

Go ahead and remove it. **T=1 is cleaner, matches the strict spec reading, and the final fitness is statistically identical.** You give up a little early-run diversity but gain spec conformance with no practical downside.

Want me to set `SELECTION_TEMPERATURE = 1.0` (or remove the temperature mechanism entirely)?

  "old_string": "def choose_pair_indices(elite_fitness: np.ndarray, n_pairs: int,\n                        rng: Generator,\n                        temperature: float = SELECTION_TEMPERATURE) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:\n    # Softmax-weighted sampling within the elite block, with replacement across pairs.\n    # Raw-fitness softmax is extremely peaked when fitness deltas are O(1+),\n    # so divide by a temperature before exponentiating to keep the selection pressure sane.\n    shifted = (elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()) / max(temperature, 1e-9)\n    probs = np.exp(shifted)\n    probs /= probs.sum()",
  "new_string": "def choose_pair_indices(elite_fitness: np.ndarray, n_pairs: int,\n                        rng: Generator) -> tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:\n    # Softmax-weighted sampling within the elite block, with replacement across pairs.\n    # Max-subtraction is a numerical-stability trick; produces identical probabilities\n    # to plain softmax but avoids overflow when fitnesses are large.\n    shifted = elite_fitness - elite_fitness.max()\n    probs = np.exp(shifted)\n    probs /= probs.sum()"
}
